                  <hi rend="ital">A single sitting.</hi> (S, L, Msb.) Ex. <foreign lang="ar">قَعَدَ قَعْدَةً وَاحِدَةً</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He sat a single sitting.</hi> (L.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">قَعْدَةُ رَجُلٍ</foreign>, see <foreign lang="ar">قِعْدَةٌ</foreign> in three places.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  And see <foreign lang="ar">قَاعِدٌ</foreign>.       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ذُو القَعْدَةِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">القِعْدَةِ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">A certain month;</hi> (S, L, K;) [<hi rend="ital">the eleventh month of the Arabian year;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">next after</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَوَّال</foreign>: (L:) so called because the Arabs [when their year was solar] used to abstain (<foreign lang="ar">يَقْعُدُونَ</foreign>) therein from journeys (L, K, * TA) and warring and plundering expeditions and laying in stores of corn and seeking pasturage, before performing the pilgrimage in the next month; (L, TA;) or because in that month they broke in the young camels (<foreign lang="ar">القِعْدَان</foreign>) for riding: (Msb, voce <foreign lang="ar">جُمَادَى</foreign>:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتُ القَعْدَةِ</foreign> (S, L, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتُ القَعَدَاتِ</foreign>; (Yoo, Msb;) but the former is the regular pl., (Yoo,) because the two words are considered as one, (Msb,) and it is the more common: (TA:) dual <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتَا القَعْدَةِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتَا القَعْدَتَيْنِ</foreign>.                   <hi rend="ital">A companion in sitting:</hi> (S, AHeyth, L, K:) of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعِيلٌ</foreign> in the sense of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مُفَاعِلٌ</foreign>. [In some copies of the K, by the omission of <foreign lang="ar">وَ</foreign>, this meaning is assigned to <foreign lang="ar">مُقَاعِدٌ</foreign>.] It is used alike as sing. and pl. and masc. and fem. (L, K) and dual also. (L.) It is said in the Kur, [l. 16,] <foreign lang="ar">عَنِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">اليَمِينِ وَعَنِ الشِمَالِ قَعِيدٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">On the right and on the left a sitter,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">guardian,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">watcher</hi>]: respecting which it is observed, that <foreign lang="ar">فَعِيلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فَعُولٌ</foreign> are of the measures used alike as sing. and dual and pl.; as in <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّا رَسُولُ رَبِّكَ</foreign>, [Kur xi. 83, accord. to one reading,] and <foreign lang="ar">وَالمَلَائِكَةُ بَعْدَ ذٰلِكَ ظَهِيرٌ</foreign>, [Kur lxvi. 4:] (S, L:) or, as the grammarians say, <foreign lang="ar">قَعِيدٌ</foreign> is understood after <foreign lang="ar">اليمين</foreign>.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35963-8" target="قعد" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> are inf. us. put in the acc. case because of a verb understood; [or rather, as it appears to me, and as I have said above, they are epithets, put in the acc. case because of the prep. <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> understood;] and the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">By thy Companion, who is the Companion of every secret,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">I will not come to thee;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">by thy Companion, &amp;c.,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by thy Watcher,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Keeper, God, I will not come to thee;</hi>] like as one says <foreign lang="ar">نَشَدْتُكَ ٱللّٰهَ</foreign>: (S, L:) some say, that <foreign lang="ar">قعيد</foreign> and
